Mean Time">GMT</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><span style="white-space:nowrap">&#160;\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;Summer (<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</span></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/UTC%2B1" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+1">UTC+1</a> (<a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">BST</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Postcodes_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Postcodes in the United Kingdom">Postcodes</a></th><td class="adr">\n<span class="postal-code"><a href="/wiki/EC_postcode_area" title="EC postcode area">EC</a>, <a href="/wiki/WC_postcode_area" title="WC postcode area">WC</a>, <a href="/wiki/E_postcode_area" title="E postcode area">E</a></span></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">Area code(s)</a></th><td>\n020</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Geocode" class="mw-redirect" title="Geocode">Geocode</a></th><td class="nickname">\n<div class="plainlist"><ul><li><span style="white-space: nowrap" class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://tools.wmflabs.org/os/coor_g/?pagename=City_of_London&amp;params=TQ32488134_region%3AGB_scale%3A25000">TQ32488134</a></span> (<a href="/wiki/British_national_grid_reference_system" class="mw-redirect" title="British national grid reference system">Grid ref.</a>)</li><li>00AA (<a Code</a>)</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">Transport for London</a> zones</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/List_of_stations_in_London_fare_zone_1" title="List of stations in London fare zone 1">Fare zone 1</a>; <a href="/wiki/London_congestion_charge" title="London congestion charge">congestion charge zone</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/List_of_law_enforcement_agencies_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="List of law enforcement agencies in the United Kingdom">Police</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Police" title="City of London Police">City of London Police</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">Patron saint</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">St. Paul</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cityoflondon.gov.uk/">cityoflondon.gov.uk</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>City of London</b> is a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_England" title="Counties of England">county</a> that contains the historic centre and the primary <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a> (CBD) of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. It constituted most of London from its <a href="/wiki/Londinium" title="Londinium">settlement</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> in the 1st century AD to the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, but the agglomeration has since grown far beyond the City\'s borders.<sup id="cite_ref-beckett_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beckett-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mills_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  The City is now only a tiny part of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_London_Built-up_Area" title="Greater London Built-up Area">metropolis of London</a>, though it remains a notable part of <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">central London</a>. Administratively, it forms one of the 33 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_England" title="Districts of England">local authority districts</a> of <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">Greater London</a>; however, the City of London is not a <a href="/wiki/London_borough" class="mw-redirect" title="London borough">London borough</a>, a status reserved for the other 32 districts (including London\'s only other city, the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">City of Westminster</a>). It is also a separate county of England, being an <a href="/wiki/Enclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Enclave">enclave</a> surrounded by Greater London. It is the smallest county in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.\n</p><p>The City of London is widely referred to simply as <b>the City</b> (differentiated from the phrase "the city of London" by capitalising <i>City</i>) and is also colloquially known as the <b>Square Mile</b>, as it is 1.12&#160;sq&#160;mi (716.80 acres; 2.90&#160;km<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> in area. Both of these terms are also often used as <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">metonyms</a> for the United Kingdom\'s trading and <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> industries, which continue a notable history of being largely based in the City.<sup id="cite_ref-Roberts2008_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts2008-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Etymology_of_London" title="Etymology of London">name <i>London</i></a> is now ordinarily used for a far wider area than just the City. <i>London</i> most often denotes the sprawling London metropolis, or the 32 London boroughs, in addition to the City of London itself. This wider usage of <i>London</i> is documented as far back as 1888, when the <a href="/wiki/County_of_London" title="County of London">County of London</a> was created.<sup id="cite_ref-Mills_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_England" title="Local government in England">local authority</a> for the City, namely the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Corporation" title="City of London Corporation">City of London Corporation</a>, is unique in the UK and has some unusual responsibilities for a local council, such as being the police authority. It is also unusual in having responsibilities and ownerships beyond its boundaries. The Corporation is headed by the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_London" title="Lord Mayor of London">Lord Mayor of the City of London</a>, an office separate from (and much older than) the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_London" title="Mayor of London">Mayor of London</a>. The current Lord Mayor, as of November 2017, is <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bowman_(Lord_Mayor_of_London)" title="Charles Bowman (Lord Mayor of London)">Charles Bowman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The City is a major business and <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Throughout the 19th century, the City was the world\'s primary business centre, and it continues to be a major meeting point for businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-world_and_its_people_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world_and_its_people-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> London came top in the <a href="/wiki/Worldwide_Centres_of_Commerce_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Worldwide Centres of Commerce Index">Worldwide Centres of Commerce Index</a>, published in 2008. The insurance industry is focused around the eastern side of the City, around <a href="/wiki/Lloyd%27s_building" title="Lloyd&#39;s building">Lloyd\'s building</a>. A secondary financial district exists outside the City, at <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf" title="Canary Wharf">Canary Wharf</a>, 2.5 miles (4&#160;km) to the east.\n</p><p>The City has a resident population of 9,401 (<a href="/wiki/Office_of_National_Statistics" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of National Statistics">ONS</a> estimate, mid-2016) but over 300,000 people commute to and work there. About three quarters of the jobs in the City of London are in the financial, professional, and associated business services sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-citylondon_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citylondon-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The legal profession forms a major component of the northern and western sides of the City, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Temple,_London" title="Temple, London">Temple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chancery_Lane" title="Chancery Lane">Chancery Lane</a> areas where the <a href="/wiki/Inns_of_Court" title="Inns of Court">Inns of Court</a> are located, of which two\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Inner_Temple" title="Inner Temple">Inner Temple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Temple" title="Middle Temple">Middle Temple</a>\xe2\x80\x94fall within the City of London boundary.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_London" title="History of London">History of London</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman London">Roman London</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Horned_helmet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Horned_helmet.jpg/220px-Horned_helmet.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Horned_helmet.jpg/330px-Horned_helmet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Horned_helmet.jpg/440px-Horned_helmet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Horned_helmet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Helmet" title="Waterloo Helmet">Waterloo Helmet</a>, c. 150\xe2\x80\x9350 BC, found in the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Wall_fragment.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/London_Wall_fragment.jpg/220px-London_Wall_fragment.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/London_Wall_fragment.jpg/330px-London_Wall_fragment.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/London_Wall_fragment.jpg/440px-London_Wall_fragment.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="563" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Wall_fragment.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A surviving fragment of the <a href="/wiki/London_Wall" title="London Wall">London Wall</a>, built around 200 AD, close to <a href="/wiki/Tower_Hill" title="Tower Hill">Tower Hill</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Known as "Londinium",  the Roman legions established on the current site of the City of London around <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span>&#160;43. Its bridge over the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a> turned the city into a <a href="#Roads">road nexus</a> and major <a href="#Port">port</a>, serving as a major commercial centre in <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman Britain</a> until its abandonment during <a href="#5th_century">the 5th century</a>. Archaeologist Leslie Wallace notes that "Because no <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Britain#Late_pre-Roman_Iron_Age_(LPRIA)" title="Prehistoric Britain">LPRIA</a> settlements or significant domestic refuse have been found in London, despite extensive archaeological excavation, arguments for a purely Roman foundation of London are now common and uncontroversial."<sup id="cite_ref-Wallace_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wallace-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At its height, the Roman city had a population of approximately 45,000\xe2\x80\x9360,000 inhabitants. Londinium was an ethnically diverse city, with inhabitants from across the Roman Empire, including natives of Britannia, <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The Romans built the <a href="/wiki/London_Wall" title="London Wall">London Wall</a> some time between 190 and 225 AD. The boundaries of the Roman city were similar to those of the City of London today, though Londinium did not extend further west than <a href="/wiki/Ludgate" title="Ludgate">Ludgate</a> or the <a href="/wiki/River_Fleet" title="River Fleet">Fleet</a>, and the mid-estuary Thames was undredged and wider than it is today thus, the City\'s shoreline was north of its present position. The Romans built a bridge across the river, as early as 50 AD, near to today\'s <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge" title="London Bridge">London Bridge</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline">Decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By the time the London Wall was constructed, the City\'s fortunes were in decline, and it faced problems of plague and fire. The Roman Empire entered a long period of <a href="/wiki/Decline_of_the_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Decline of the Roman Empire">instability and decline</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Carausian_Revolt" title="Carausian Revolt">Carausian Revolt</a> in Britain. In the 3rd and 4th centuries, the city was under attack from <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a>, Scots, and <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxon</a> raiders. The decline continued, both for Londinium and the Empire, and in 410 AD the Romans withdrew entirely from Britain. Many of the Roman public buildings in Londinium by this time had fallen into decay and disuse, and gradually after the formal withdrawal the city became almost (if not, at times, entirely) uninhabited. The centre of trade and population moved away from the walled Londinium to <a href="/wiki/Lundenwic" class="mw-redirect" title="Lundenwic">Lundenwic</a> ("London market"), a settlement to the west, roughly in the modern day <a href="/wiki/Strand,_London" title="Strand, London">Strand</a>/<a href="/wiki/Aldwych" title="Aldwych">Aldwych</a>/<a href="/wiki/Covent_Garden" title="Covent Garden">Covent Garden</a> area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglo-Saxon_restoration">Anglo-Saxon restoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Anglo-Saxon restoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_London" title="Anglo-Saxon London">Anglo-Saxon London</a></div>\n<p>During the Anglo-Saxon <a href="/wiki/Heptarchy" title="Heptarchy">Heptarchy</a>, the London area came in turn under the Kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Essex" title="Kingdom of Essex">Essex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercia" title="Mercia">Mercia</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a>, though from the mid 8th century it was frequently under the control or threat of the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Southwark_Bridge_City_Plaque.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Southwark_Bridge_City_Plaque.JPG/220px-Southwark_Bridge_City_Plaque.JPG" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Southwark_Bridge_City_Plaque.JPG/330px-Southwark_Bridge_City_Plaque.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Southwark_Bridge_City_Plaque.JPG/440px-Southwark_Bridge_City_Plaque.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1835" data-file-height="1203" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southwark_Bridge_City_Plaque.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plaque near <a href="/wiki/Southwark_Bridge" title="Southwark Bridge">Southwark Bridge</a> noting the activities around the time of <a href="/wiki/Alfred_the_Great" title="Alfred the Great">King Alfred</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Bede" title="Bede">Bede</a> records that in 604 AD <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Canterbury" title="Augustine of Canterbury">St Augustine</a> consecrated <a href="/wiki/Mellitus" title="Mellitus">Mellitus</a> as the first bishop to the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxon</a> kingdom of the <a href="/wiki/East_Saxons" class="mw-redirect" title="East Saxons">East Saxons</a> and their king, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A6berht_of_Essex" title="S\xc3\xa6berht of Essex">S\xc3\xa6berht</a>. S\xc3\xa6berht\'s uncle and overlord, <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelberht_of_Kent" title="\xc3\x86thelberht of Kent">\xc3\x86thelberht</a>, king of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kent" title="Kingdom of Kent">Kent</a>, built a church dedicated to St Paul in London, as the seat of the new bishop.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It is assumed, although unproven, that this first Anglo-Saxon cathedral stood on the same site as the later medieval and the present cathedrals.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Alfred_the_Great" title="Alfred the Great">Alfred the Great</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_of_Wessex" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Wessex">King of Wessex</a> and arguably the first king of the "English", occupied and began the resettlement of the old <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> walled area, in 886, and appointed his son-in-law <a href="/wiki/Earl_Aethelred_of_Mercia" class="mw-redirect" title="Earl Aethelred of Mercia">Earl \xc3\x86thelred of Mercia</a> over it as part of their reconquest of the Viking occupied parts of England. The refortified Anglo-Saxon settlement was known as <a href="/wiki/Lundenburh" class="mw-redirect" title="Lundenburh">Lundenburh</a> ("London Fort", a <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a>). The historian Asser said that "Alfred, king of the Anglo-Saxons, restored the city of London splendidly&#160;... and made it habitable once more."<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Alfred\'s "restoration" entailed reoccupying and refurbishing the nearly deserted Roman walled city, building quays along the Thames, and laying a new city street plan.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Alfred\'s taking of London and the rebuilding of the old Roman city was a turning point in history, not only as the permanent establishment of the City of London, but also as part of a unifying moment in early England, with Wessex becoming the dominant English kingdom and the repelling (to some degree) of the Viking occupation and raids. While London, and indeed England, were afterwards subjected to further periods of Viking and Danish raids and occupation, the establishment of the City of London and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> prevailed.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 10th century, <a href="/wiki/Athelstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Athelstan">Athelstan</a> permitted eight <a href="/wiki/Royal_mint" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal mint">mints</a> to be established, compared with six in his capital, <a href="/wiki/Winchester,_Hampshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Winchester, Hampshire">Winchester</a>, indicating the wealth of the city. <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge" title="London Bridge">London Bridge</a>, which had fallen into ruin following the Roman evacuation and abandonment of Londinium, was rebuilt by the Saxons, but was periodically destroyed by Viking raids and storms.\n</p><p>As the focus of trade and population was moved back to within the old Roman walls, the older Saxon settlement of Lundenwic was largely abandoned and gained the name of <i>Ealdwic</i> (the "old settlement"). The name survives today as <a href="/wiki/Aldwych" title="Aldwych">Aldwych</a> (the "old market-place"), a name of a street and an area of the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">City of Westminster</a> between <a href="/wiki/Westminster" title="Westminster">Westminster</a> and the City of London.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_era">Medieval era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Medieval era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_London,_1300.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Map_of_London%2C_1300.svg/220px-Map_of_London%2C_1300.svg.png" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Map_of_London%2C_1300.svg/330px-Map_of_London%2C_1300.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Map_of_London%2C_1300.svg/440px-Map_of_London%2C_1300.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="842" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_London,_1300.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of London in about 1300</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DeathWatTyler.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/DeathWatTyler.jpg/220px-DeathWatTyler.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/DeathWatTyler.jpg/330px-DeathWatTyler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/DeathWatTyler.jpg/440px-DeathWatTyler.jpg 2x" data-file-width="682" data-file-height="499" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DeathWatTyler.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A pivotal event during the <a href="/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt" title="Peasants&#39; Revolt">Peasants\' Revolt</a>, 1381: their leader <a href="/wiki/Wat_Tyler" title="Wat Tyler">Wat Tyler</a> is stabbed by <a href="/wiki/William_Walworth" title="William Walworth">William Walworth</a>, Lord Mayor</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Norman_and_Medieval_London" title="Norman and Medieval London">Norman and Medieval London</a></div>\n<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hastings" title="Battle of Hastings">Battle of Hastings</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">William the Conqueror</a> marched on London <i>(reaching as far as <a href="/wiki/Southwark" title="Southwark">Southwark</a>)</i>, but failed to get across London Bridge or to defeat the Londoners. He eventually crossed the River Thames at <a href="/wiki/Wallingford,_Oxfordshire" title="Wallingford, Oxfordshire">Wallingford</a>, pillaging the land as he went. Rather than continuing the war, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_the_%C3%86theling" class="mw-redirect" title="Edgar the \xc3\x86theling">Edgar the \xc3\x86theling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edwin,_Earl_of_Mercia" title="Edwin, Earl of Mercia">Edwin of Mercia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morcar" title="Morcar">Morcar</a> of Northumbria surrendered at <a href="/wiki/Berkhamsted" title="Berkhamsted">Berkhamsted</a>. William granted the citizens of London a charter in 1075; the City was one of a few examples of the English retaining some authority. The City was not covered by the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a>.\n</p><p>William built three castles nearby, to keep Londoners subdued:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Baynard%27s_Castle" title="Baynard&#39;s Castle">Baynard\'s Castle</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Montfichet%27s_Tower" title="Montfichet&#39;s Tower">Montfichet\'s Tower</a></li></ul>\n<p>About 1130, <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_England" title="Henry I of England">Henry I</a> granted a <a href="/wiki/Shrievalty_of_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Shrievalty of London">sheriff</a> to the people of London, along with control of the county of <a href="/wiki/Middlesex" title="Middlesex">Middlesex</a>: this meant that the two entities were regarded as one administratively (not that the county was a dependency of the City) until the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1888" title="Local Government Act 1888">Local Government Act 1888</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vch_middlesex_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vch_middlesex-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> By 1141 the whole body of the citizenry was considered to constitute a single community. This \'commune\' was the origin of the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Corporation" title="City of London Corporation">City of London Corporation</a> and the citizens gained the right to appoint, with the king\'s consent, a Mayor in 1189\xe2\x80\x94and to directly elect the Mayor from 1215.\n</p><p>From medieval times, the City has been composed of <a href="/wiki/Wards_of_the_City_of_London" title="Wards of the City of London">25 ancient wards</a>, each headed by an <a href="/wiki/Alderman" title="Alderman">Alderman</a>, who chairs <a href="/wiki/Wardmote" title="Wardmote">Wardmotes</a>, which still take place at least annually. A <a href="/wiki/Folkmoot" class="mw-redirect" title="Folkmoot">Folkmoot</a>, for the whole of the City held at the outdoor cross of <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul&#39;s Cathedral">St Paul\'s Cathedral</a>, was formerly also held. Many of the medieval offices and traditions continue to the present day, demonstrating the unique nature of the City and its <a href="/wiki/Corporation_of_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporation of London">Corporation</a>.\n</p><p>In 1381, the <a href="/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt" title="Peasants&#39; Revolt">Peasants\' Revolt</a> affected London. The rebels took the City and the Tower of London, but the rebellion ended after its leader, Wat Tyler, was killed during a confrontation that included Lord Mayor <a href="/wiki/William_Walworth" title="William Walworth">William Walworth</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Civitas_Londinium_or_The_Agas_Map_of_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Civitas_Londinium_or_The_Agas_Map_of_London.jpg/220px-Civitas_Londinium_or_The_Agas_Map_of_London.jpg" width="220" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Civitas_Londinium_or_The_Agas_Map_of_London.jpg/330px-Civitas_Londinium_or_The_Agas_Map_of_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Civitas_Londinium_or_The_Agas_Map_of_London.jpg/440px-Civitas_Londinium_or_The_Agas_Map_of_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4730" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Civitas_Londinium_or_The_Agas_Map_of_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Woodcut_map_of_London" title="Woodcut map of London">"Woodcut" map of London</a>, dating from the 1560s</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_fire_of_london_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Great_fire_of_london_map.png/220px-Great_fire_of_london_map.png" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Great_fire_of_london_map.png/330px-Great_fire_of_london_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Great_fire_of_london_map.png/440px-Great_fire_of_london_map.png 2x" data-file-width="2549" data-file-height="1612" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_fire_of_london_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the extent of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_London" title="Great Fire of London">Great Fire of London</a>, which destroyed nearly 80% of the City</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_Fire_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Great_Fire_London.jpg/220px-Great_Fire_London.jpg" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Great_Fire_London.jpg/330px-Great_Fire_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Great_Fire_London.jpg/440px-Great_Fire_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1021" data-file-height="594" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_Fire_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1666 Great Fire as depicted in a 17th-century painting: it depicts Old London Bridge, churches, houses, and the Tower of London as seen from a boat near Tower Wharf</div></div></div>\n<p>The City was burnt severely on a number of occasions, the worst being in 1123 and (more famously) in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_London" title="Great Fire of London">Great Fire of London</a> in 1666. Both of these fires were referred to as <i>the</i> Great Fire. After the fire of 1666, a number of plans were drawn up to remodel the City and its street pattern into a <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">renaissance</a>-style city with planned urban blocks, squares and boulevards. These plans were almost entirely not taken up, and the medieval street pattern re-emerged almost intact.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">Early modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By the late 16th century, London increasingly became a major centre for banking, international trade and commerce. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Exchange,_London" title="Royal Exchange, London">Royal Exchange</a> was founded in 1565 by Sir <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Gresham" title="Thomas Gresham">Thomas Gresham</a> as a centre of commerce for London\'s merchants, and gained Royal patronage in 1571. Although no longer used for its original purpose, its location at the corner of <a href="/wiki/Cornhill,_London" title="Cornhill, London">Cornhill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Threadneedle_Street" title="Threadneedle Street">Threadneedle Street</a> continues to be the geographical centre of the City\'s core of banking and financial services, with the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> moving to its present site in 1734, opposite the Royal Exchange on Threadneedle Street. Immediately to the south of Cornhill, <a href="/wiki/Lombard_Street,_London" title="Lombard Street, London">Lombard Street</a> was the location from 1691 of <a href="/wiki/Lloyd%27s_Coffee_House" title="Lloyd&#39;s Coffee House">Lloyd\'s Coffee House</a>, which became the world-leading insurance market. London\'s insurance sector continues to be based in the area, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Lime_Street_(ward)" title="Lime Street (ward)">Lime Street</a>.\n</p><p>In 1708, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wren" title="Christopher Wren">Christopher Wren</a>\'s masterpiece, <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul&#39;s Cathedral">St Paul\'s Cathedral</a>, was completed on his birthday. The first service had been held on 2 December 1697, more than 10 years earlier. It replaced the original St Paul\'s, which had been completely destroyed in the Great Fire of London, and is considered to be one of the finest cathedrals in Britain and a fine example of <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque architecture</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth_of_London">Growth of London</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Growth of London">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 18th century was a period of rapid growth for London, reflecting an increasing national population, the early stirrings of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, and London\'s role at the centre of the evolving <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. The urban area expanded beyond the borders of the City of London, most notably during this period towards the <a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westminster" title="Westminster">Westminster</a>.\n</p><p>Expansion continued and became more rapid by the beginning of the 19th century, with London growing in all directions. To the <a href="/wiki/East_End_of_London" title="East End of London">East</a> the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_London" title="Port of London">Port of London</a> grew rapidly during the century, with the construction of many docks, needed as the Thames at the City could not cope with the volume of trade. The arrival of the railways and the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">Tube</a> meant that London could expand over a much greater area. By the mid-19th century, with London still rapidly expanding in population and area, the City had already become only a small part of the wider metropolis.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_and_20th_centuries">19th and 20th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 19th and 20th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>An attempt was made in 1894 with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Commission_on_the_Amalgamation_of_the_City_and_County_of_London" title="Royal Commission on the Amalgamation of the City and County of London">Royal Commission on the Amalgamation of the City and County of London</a> to end the distinction between the City and the surrounding County of London, but a change of government at Westminster meant the option was not taken up. The City as a distinct <a href="/wiki/Polity" title="Polity">polity</a> survived despite its position within the London conurbation and <a href="/wiki/History_of_local_government_in_London" title="History of local government in London">numerous local government reforms</a>. Supporting this status, the City was a special <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_borough" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary borough">parliamentary borough</a> that elected four members to the <a href="/wiki/Unreformed_House_of_Commons" title="Unreformed House of Commons">unreformed House of Commons</a>, who were retained after the <a href="/wiki/Reform_Act_1832" title="Reform Act 1832">Reform Act 1832</a>; reduced to two under the <a href="/wiki/Redistribution_of_Seats_Act_1885" title="Redistribution of Seats Act 1885">Redistribution of Seats Act 1885</a>; and ceased to be a separate constituency under the <a href="/wiki/Representation_of_the_People_Act_1948" title="Representation of the People Act 1948">Representation of the People Act 1948</a>. Since then the City is a minority (in terms of population and area) of the <a href="/wiki/Cities_of_London_and_Westminster" class="mw-redirect" title="Cities of London and Westminster">Cities of London and Westminster</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pauls_Cathedral_in_1896.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/St_Pauls_Cathedral_in_1896.JPG/220px-St_Pauls_Cathedral_in_1896.JPG" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/St_Pauls_Cathedral_in_1896.JPG/330px-St_Pauls_Cathedral_in_1896.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/St_Pauls_Cathedral_in_1896.JPG/440px-St_Pauls_Cathedral_in_1896.JPG 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pauls_Cathedral_in_1896.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul&#39;s Cathedral">St Paul\'s Cathedral</a>, 1896.</div></div></div>\n<p>The City\'s population fell rapidly in the 19th century and through most of the 20th century, as people moved outwards in all directions to London\'s vast <a href="/wiki/Metro-land" title="Metro-land">suburbs</a>, and many residential buildings were demolished to make way for office blocks. Like many areas of London and other British cities, the City fell victim to large scale and highly destructive aerial bombing during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, especially in <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a>. Whilst St Paul\'s Cathedral survived the onslaught, large swathes of the area did not and the particularly heavy raids of late December 1940 led to a <a href="/wiki/Firestorm" title="Firestorm">firestorm</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Second_Great_Fire_of_London" title="Second Great Fire of London">Second Great Fire of London</a>.\n</p><p>There was a major rebuilding programme in the decades following the war, in some parts (such as at the Barbican) dramatically altering the urban landscape. But the destruction of the older historic fabric allowed the construction of modern and larger-scale developments, whereas in those parts not so badly affected by bomb damage the City retains its older character of smaller buildings. The street pattern, which is still largely medieval, was altered slightly in places, although there is a more recent trend of reversing some of the post-war modernist changes made, such as at <a href="/wiki/Paternoster_Square" title="Paternoster Square">Paternoster Square</a>.\n</p><p>The City suffered terrorist attacks including the <a href="/wiki/1993_Bishopsgate_bombing" title="1993 Bishopsgate bombing">1993 Bishopsgate bombing</a>  (<a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">IRA</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/7_July_2005_London_bombings" title="7 July 2005 London bombings">7 July 2005 London bombings</a> (<a href="/wiki/Islamic_terrorism" title="Islamic terrorism">Islamist</a>). In response to the 1993 bombing, a system of road barriers, checkpoints and surveillance cameras referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Ring_of_steel_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ring of steel (London)">ring of steel</a>" has been maintained to control entry points to the City.\n</p><p>The 1970s saw the construction of tall office buildings including the 600-foot (183&#160;m), 47-storey <a href="/wiki/Natwest_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Natwest Tower">Natwest Tower</a>, the first skyscraper in the UK. Office space development has intensified especially in the central, northern and eastern parts, with skyscrapers including <a href="/wiki/30_St_Mary_Axe" title="30 St Mary Axe">30 St. Mary Axe</a> ("the Gherkin"\'), <a href="/wiki/122_Leadenhall_Street" title="122 Leadenhall Street">Leadenhall Building</a> ("the Cheesegrater"), <a href="/wiki/20_Fenchurch_Street" title="20 Fenchurch Street">20 Fenchurch Street</a> ("the Walkie-Talkie"), the <a href="/wiki/Broadgate_Tower" title="Broadgate Tower">Broadgate Tower</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Heron_Tower" title="Heron Tower">Heron Tower</a>, the tallest in the City. Another skyscraper, <a href="/wiki/22_Bishopsgate" title="22 Bishopsgate">22 Bishopsgate</a>, is under construction.\n</p><p>The main residential section of the City today is the <a href="/wiki/Barbican_Estate" title="Barbican Estate">Barbican Estate</a>, constructed between 1965 and 1976. The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_London" title="Museum of London">Museum of London</a> is based there, as are a number of other services provided by the Corporation.\n</p><p><i>For a history of the etymology behind the City\'s streets see: <a href="/wiki/Street_names_of_the_City_of_London" title="Street names of the City of London">Street names of the City of London</a></i>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guildhall,_Londres,_Inglaterra,_2014-08-11,_DD_139.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" data-file-width="4959" data-file-height="3591" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guildhall,_Londres,_Inglaterra,_2014-08-11,_DD_139.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Guildhall,_London" title="Guildhall, London">Guildhall</a> is the ceremonial and administrative centre of the City.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_MMB_%C2%BB2K9_Mansion_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/London_MMB_%C2%BB2K9_Mansion_House.jpg/220px-London_MMB_%C2%BB2K9_Mansion_House.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/London_MMB_%C2%BB2K9_Mansion_House.jpg/330px-London_MMB_%C2%BB2K9_Mansion_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/London_MMB_%C2%BB2K9_Mansion_House.jpg/440px-London_MMB_%C2%BB2K9_Mansion_House.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3924" data-file-height="2997" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_MMB_%C2%BB2K9_Mansion_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mansion_House,_London" title="Mansion House, London">Mansion House</a> is the official residence of the Lord Mayor.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lord_Mayor_of_London_-_John_Stuttard_-_Nov_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Lord_Mayor_of_London_-_John_Stuttard_-_Nov_2006.jpg/220px-Lord_Mayor_of_London_-_John_Stuttard_-_Nov_2006.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Lord_Mayor_of_London_-_John_Stuttard_-_Nov_2006.jpg/330px-Lord_Mayor_of_London_-_John_Stuttard_-_Nov_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Lord_Mayor_of_London_-_John_Stuttard_-_Nov_2006.jpg/440px-Lord_Mayor_of_London_-_John_Stuttard_-_Nov_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lord_Mayor_of_London_-_John_Stuttard_-_Nov_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Stuttard" title="John Stuttard">John Stuttard</a>, Lord Mayor of the City of London 2006\xe2\x80\x932007, during the Lord Mayor\'s Show of 2006.</div></div></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Accuracy dispute" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ambox_contradict.svg/40px-Ambox_contradict.svg.png" title="Accuracy dispute" width="40" height="40"
