class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>appears to contradict the  article <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Corporation" title="City of London Corporation">City of London Corporation</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please see discussion on the linked <a href="/wiki/Talk:City_of_London" title="Talk:City of London">talk page</a>.</span>  <small><i>(August 2013)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Corporation" title="City of London Corporation">City of London Corporation</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_local_government_in_England#The_City_of_London" title="History of local government in England">History of local government in England \xc2\xa7&#160;The City of London</a></div>\n<p>The City has a unique political status, a legacy of its uninterrupted integrity as a corporate city since the <a href="/wiki/Heptarchy" title="Heptarchy">Anglo-Saxon period</a> and its singular relationship with the <a href="/wiki/British_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarchy">Crown</a>. Historically its system of government was not unusual, but it was not reformed by the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Reform_Act_1835" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal Reform Act 1835">Municipal Reform Act 1835</a> and little changed by later reforms.\n</p><p>It is administered by the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Corporation" title="City of London Corporation">City of London Corporation</a>, headed by the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_London" title="Lord Mayor of London">Lord Mayor of London</a> (<i>not the same as the more recent <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_London" title="Mayor of London">Mayor of London</a></i>), which is responsible for a number of functions and has interests in land beyond the City\'s boundaries. Unlike other English local authorities, the Corporation has two council bodies: the (now largely ceremonial) <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Aldermen" title="Court of Aldermen">Court of Aldermen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Common_Council" title="Court of Common Council">Court of Common Council</a>. The Court of Aldermen represents the wards, with each ward (irrespective of size) returning one Alderman. The chief executive of the Corporation holds the ancient office of <a href="/wiki/Town_Clerk_of_London" title="Town Clerk of London">Town Clerk of London</a>.\n</p><p>The City is a <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">ceremonial county</a> which has a Commission of Lieutenancy headed by the Lord Mayor instead of a <a href="/wiki/Lord-Lieutenant" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord-Lieutenant">Lord-Lieutenant</a> and has <a href="/wiki/Sheriffs_of_the_City_of_London" title="Sheriffs of the City of London">two Sheriffs</a> instead of a <a href="/wiki/High_Sheriff" class="mw-redirect" title="High Sheriff">High Sheriff</a> (see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Sheriffs_of_London" title="List of Sheriffs of London">list of Sheriffs of London</a>), quasi-judicial offices appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Livery_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Livery Company">Livery Companies</a>, an ancient political system based on the representation and <a href="/wiki/Guild" title="Guild">protection of trades (Guilds)</a>. Senior members of the Livery Companies are known as <a href="/wiki/Liveryman" class="mw-redirect" title="Liveryman">Liverymen</a> and form the Common Hall, which chooses the Lord Mayor, the Sheriffs and certain other officers.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wards">Wards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Wards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wards_of_the_City_of_London" title="Wards of the City of London">Wards of the City of London</a></div>\n<p>The City is made up of <a href="/wiki/Category:Wards_of_the_City_of_London" title="Category:Wards of the City of London">25 wards</a>. They are survivors of the medieval government system that allowed a very local area to exist as a self-governing unit within the wider city.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> They can be described as electoral/political divisions; ceremonial, geographic and administrative entities; sub-divisions of the City. Each ward has an <a href="/wiki/Alderman" title="Alderman">Alderman</a>, who until the mid-1960s<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> held office for life but since put themselves up for re-election at least every 6 years. Wards continue to have a <a href="/wiki/Beadle" title="Beadle">Beadle</a>, an ancient position which is now largely ceremonial whose main remaining function is the running of an annual <a href="/wiki/Wardmote" title="Wardmote">Wardmote</a> of electors, representatives and officials.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> At the Wardmote the ward\'s Alderman appoints at least one Deputy for the year ahead. Each ward also has a Ward Club, which is similar to a <a href="/wiki/Residents%27_association" title="Residents&#39; association">residents\' association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The wards are ancient and their number has changed three times since <a href="/wiki/Time_immemorial" title="Time immemorial">time immemorial</a>\n</p>\n<ul><li>in 1394 <a href="/wiki/Farringdon,_London" title="Farringdon, London">Farringdon</a> was divided into Farringdon Within and Farringdon Without</li>\n<li>in 1550 the ward of Bridge Without, <a href="/wiki/Southwark" title="Southwark">south of the river</a>, was created, the ward of Bridge becoming Bridge Within;<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>in 1978 these Bridge wards were merged as <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(ward)" title="Bridge (ward)">Bridge</a> ward.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_Ward_Map,_1870.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/City_of_London_Ward_Map%2C_1870.svg/220px-City_of_London_Ward_Map%2C_1870.svg.png" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/City_of_London_Ward_Map%2C_1870.svg/330px-City_of_London_Ward_Map%2C_1870.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/City_of_London_Ward_Map%2C_1870.svg/440px-City_of_London_Ward_Map%2C_1870.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1213" data-file-height="801" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_Ward_Map,_1870.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of the wards as they were in the late 19th century.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_UK_labelled_ward_map_2003.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/City_of_London_UK_labelled_ward_map_2003.svg/220px-City_of_London_UK_labelled_ward_map_2003.svg.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/City_of_London_UK_labelled_ward_map_2003.svg/330px-City_of_London_UK_labelled_ward_map_2003.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/City_of_London_UK_labelled_ward_map_2003.svg/440px-City_of_London_UK_labelled_ward_map_2003.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1213" data-file-height="907" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_UK_labelled_ward_map_2003.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of the wards since 2003</div></div></div>\n<p>Following boundary changes in 1994, and later reform of the business vote in the City, there was a major boundary and electoral representation revision of the wards in 2003, and they were reviewed again in 2010 for change in 2013, though not to such a dramatic extent. The review was conducted by senior officers of the Corporation and senior judges of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bailey" title="Old Bailey">Old Bailey</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> the wards are reviewed by this process to avoid <a href="/wiki/Malapportionment" class="mw-redirect" title="Malapportionment">malapportionment</a>. The procedure of review is unique in the United Kingdom as it is not conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a> or a local government boundary commission every 8 to 12 years, which is the case for all other <a href="/wiki/Wards_and_electoral_divisions_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Wards and electoral divisions of the United Kingdom">wards in Great Britain</a>. Particular churches, <a href="/wiki/Livery_company" title="Livery company">livery company</a> halls and other historic buildings and structures are associated with a ward, such as St Paul\'s Cathedral with <a href="/wiki/Castle_Baynard" title="Castle Baynard">Castle Baynard</a>, and London Bridge with Bridge; boundary changes in 2003 removed some of these historic connections.\n</p><p>Each ward elects an <a href="/wiki/Alderman" title="Alderman">Alderman</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Aldermen" title="Court of Aldermen">Court of Aldermen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Commoners" class="mw-redirect" title="Commoners">Commoners</a> (the City equivalent of a <a href="/wiki/Councillor" title="Councillor">Councillor</a>) to the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Common_Council" title="Court of Common Council">Court of Common Council</a> of the Corporation. Only electors who are <a href="/wiki/Freeman_of_the_City_of_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Freeman of the City of London">Freemen of the City of London</a> are eligible to stand. The number of Commoners a ward sends to the Common Council varies from two to ten, depending on the number of electors in each ward. Since the 2003 review it has been agreed that the four more residential wards: <a href="/wiki/Portsoken" title="Portsoken">Portsoken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queenhithe" title="Queenhithe">Queenhithe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aldersgate" title="Aldersgate">Aldersgate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cripplegate" title="Cripplegate">Cripplegate</a> together elect 20 of the 100 Commoners, whereas the business-dominated remainder elect the remaining 80 Commoners. 2003 and 2013 boundary changes have increased the residential emphasis of the mentioned four wards.\n</p><p>Census data provides eight nominal rather than 25 real wards, all of varying size and population. Being subject to renaming and definition at any time, these census \'wards\' are notable in that four of the eight wards accounted for 67% of the \'square mile\' and held 86% of the population, and these were in fact similar to and named after four City of London wards:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="max-width:50em;">\n<caption>Extract of census \'wards\' where approximate to underlying legal wards<sup id="cite_ref-ons_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ons-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Census ward\n</th>\n<th>% of the City of London\n</th>\n<th>Residents\n</th>\n<th>% of built-upon land: commercial\n</th>\n<th>% residential\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Cripplegate [east half of <a href="/wiki/Barbican_Estate" title="Barbican Estate">Barbican</a> neighbourhood]</td>\n<td>10.0%</td>\n<td>2,782</td>\n<td>79%</td>\n<td>21%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Aldersgate [west half of Barbican neighbourhood]</td>\n<td>4.5%</td>\n<td>1,465</td>\n<td>81%</td>\n<td>19%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Farringdon Without [and much of Castle Baynard]</td>\n<td>22.1%</td>\n<td>1,099</td>\n<td>90%</td>\n<td>10%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Portsoken [contains <a href="/wiki/Aldgate_tube_station" title="Aldgate tube station">Aldgate Underground station</a>]</td>\n<td>6.6%</td>\n<td>985</td>\n<td>86%</td>\n<td>14%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The City has a unique electoral system. Most of its voters are representatives of businesses and other bodies that occupy premises in the City. Its ancient wards have very unequal numbers of voters. In elections, both the businesses based in the City and the residents of the City vote.\n</p><p>The City of London Corporation was not reformed by the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporations_Act_1835" title="Municipal Corporations Act 1835">Municipal Corporations Act 1835</a>, because it had a more extensive electoral franchise than any other borough or city; in fact, it widened this further with its own equivalent legislation allowing one to become a <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_City" title="Freedom of the City">freeman</a> without being a <a href="/wiki/Liveryman" class="mw-redirect" title="Liveryman">liveryman</a>. In 1801, the City had a population of about 130,000, but increasing development of the City as a central business district led to this falling to below 5,000 after the Second World War.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It has risen slightly to around 9,000 since, largely due to the development of the <a href="/wiki/Barbican_Estate" title="Barbican Estate">Barbican Estate</a>. In 2009, the business vote was about 24,000, greatly exceeding residential voters.<sup id="cite_ref-tribune_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tribune-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> As the City of London Corporation has not been affected by other municipal legislation over the period of time since then, its electoral practice has become increasingly anomalous. Uniquely for city or borough elections, its elections remain independent-dominated.\n</p><p>The business or "<a href="/wiki/Non-residential_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-residential vote">non-residential vote</a>" was abolished in other UK local council elections by the <a href="/wiki/Representation_of_the_People_Act_1969" title="Representation of the People Act 1969">Representation of the People Act 1969</a>, but was preserved in the City of London. The principal reason given by successive UK governments for retaining this mechanism for giving businesses representation, is that the City is "primarily a place for doing business".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> About 330,000 non-residents constitute the day-time population and use most of its services, far outnumbering residents, who number around 7,000 (2011). By contrast, opponents of the retention of the business vote argue that it is a cause of institutional inertia.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_(Ward_Elections)_Act_2002" title="City of London (Ward Elections) Act 2002">City of London (Ward Elections) Act 2002</a>, a private Act of Parliament,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> reformed the voting system and greatly increased the business franchise, allowing many more businesses to be represented. Under the new system, the number of non-resident voters has doubled from 16,000 to 32,000. Previously disenfranchised firms (and other organisations) are entitled to nominate voters, in addition to those already represented, and all such bodies are now required to choose their voters in a representative fashion. Bodies employing fewer than ten people may appoint one voter; those employing ten to 50 people one voter for every five employees; those employing more than 50 people ten voters and one additional voter for each 50 employees beyond the first 50. The Act also removed other anomalies which had been unchanged since the 1850s.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Temple">The Temple</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The Temple">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Inner_Temple" title="Inner Temple">Inner Temple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Temple" title="Middle Temple">Middle Temple</a> (which neighbour each other) are two of the few remaining <a href="/wiki/Liberty_(division)" title="Liberty (division)">liberties</a>, an old name for a geographic division. They are independent <a href="/wiki/Extra-parochial_area" title="Extra-parochial area">extra-parochial areas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> historically not governed by the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Corporation" title="City of London Corporation">City of London Corporation</a><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> (and are today regarded as local authorities for most purposes<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>) and equally outside the <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_jurisdiction" title="Ecclesiastical jurisdiction">ecclesiastical jurisdiction</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_London" title="Bishop of London">Bishop of London</a>. They are within the boundaries and liberties of the City, but can be thought of as independent <a href="/wiki/Enclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Enclave">enclaves</a>. They are both part of <a href="/wiki/Farringdon_Without" title="Farringdon Without">Farringdon Without</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_functions">Other functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leadenhall_Market_In_London_-_Feb_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Leadenhall_Market_In_London_-_Feb_2006.jpg/220px-Leadenhall_Market_In_London_-_Feb_2006.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Leadenhall_Market_In_London_-_Feb_2006.jpg/330px-Leadenhall_Market_In_London_-_Feb_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Leadenhall_Market_In_London_-_Feb_2006.jpg/440px-Leadenhall_Market_In_London_-_Feb_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1782" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leadenhall_Market_In_London_-_Feb_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leadenhall_Market" title="Leadenhall Market">Leadenhall Market</a> is a historic market nestled between <a href="/wiki/Gracechurch_Street" title="Gracechurch Street">Gracechurch Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lime_Street,_London" title="Lime Street, London">Lime Street</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Within the City, the Corporation owns and runs both <a href="/wiki/Smithfield_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="Smithfield Market">Smithfield Market</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leadenhall_Market" title="Leadenhall Market">Leadenhall Market</a>. It owns land beyond its boundaries, including <a href="/wiki/Corporation_of_London_open_spaces" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporation of London open spaces">open spaces</a> (parks, forests and commons) in and around Greater London, including most of <a href="/wiki/Epping_Forest" title="Epping Forest">Epping Forest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hampstead_Heath" title="Hampstead Heath">Hampstead Heath</a>. <a href="/wiki/The_Honourable_The_Irish_Society" title="The Honourable The Irish Society">The Honourable The Irish Society</a>, a body closely linked with the Corporation, also owns many public spaces in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. The Corporation owns <a href="/wiki/Old_Spitalfields_Market" title="Old Spitalfields Market">Old Spitalfields Market</a> and <a href="/wiki/Billingsgate_Fish_Market" title="Billingsgate Fish Market">Billingsgate Fish Market</a>, in the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Tower_Hamlets" title="London Borough of Tower Hamlets">London Borough of Tower Hamlets</a>. It owns and helps fund the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bailey" title="Old Bailey">Old Bailey</a>, the Central Criminal Court for <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>, as a gift to the nation, having begun as the City and Middlesex Sessions.\n</p><p>The City has its own independent police force, the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Police" title="City of London Police">City of London Police</a>\xe2\x80\x94the Common Council (the main body of the Corporation) is the <a href="/wiki/Police_authority" title="Police authority">police authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The rest of Greater London is policed by the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police_Service" title="Metropolitan Police Service">Metropolitan Police Service</a>, based at <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Yard" title="Scotland Yard">New Scotland Yard</a>.\n</p><p>The City has one hospital, <a href="/wiki/St_Bartholomew%27s_Hospital" title="St Bartholomew&#39;s Hospital">St Bartholomew\'s Hospital</a>, also known as \'Barts\'. Founded in 1123, it is located at <a href="/wiki/Smithfield,_London" title="Smithfield, London">Smithfield</a>, and is undergoing a long-awaited regeneration after doubts as to its continuing use during the 1990s.\n</p><p>The City is the third largest UK patron of the arts. It oversees the <a href="/wiki/Barbican_Centre" title="Barbican Centre">Barbican Centre</a> and subsidises several important performing arts companies.\n</p><p>The London Port Health Authority, which is the responsibility of the Corporation, is responsible for all port health functions on the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_London" title="Port of London">tidal part of the Thames</a>, including various seaports and <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">London City Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The Corporation oversees the running of the <a href="/wiki/Bridge_House_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Bridge House Trust">Bridge House Trust</a>, which maintains <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge" title="London Bridge">London Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_Bridge" title="Blackfriars Bridge">Blackfriars Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southwark_Bridge" title="Southwark Bridge">Southwark Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tower_Bridge" title="Tower Bridge">Tower Bridge</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Bridge_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Bridge (London)">Millennium Bridge</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_City_of_London" title="Flag of the City of London">City\'s flag</a> flies over Tower Bridge, although neither footing is in the City.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_boundary_of_the_City">The boundary of the City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The boundary of the City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1304788.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/City_of_London_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1304788.jpg/200px-City_of_London_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1304788.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/City_of_London_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1304788.jpg/300px-City_of_London_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1304788.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/City_of_London_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1304788.jpg/400px-City_of_London_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1304788.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1304788.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>City of London welcome sign</div></div></div>\n<p>The size of the City was constrained by a defensive perimeter wall, known as <a href="/wiki/London_Wall" title="London Wall">London Wall</a>, which was built by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> in the late 2nd century to protect their strategic port city. However the boundaries of the City of London no longer coincide with the old city wall, as the City expanded its jurisdiction slightly over time. During the <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> era, the City\'s jurisdiction expanded westwards, crossing the historic western border of the original settlement\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/River_Fleet" title="River Fleet">River Fleet</a>\xe2\x80\x94along <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Street" title="Fleet Street">Fleet Street</a> to <a href="/wiki/Temple_Bar,_London" title="Temple Bar, London">Temple Bar</a>. The City also took in the other "City bars" which were situated just beyond the old walled area, such as at Holborn, Aldersgate, Bishopsgate and Aldgate. These were the important entrances to the City and their control was vital in maintaining the City\'s special privileges over certain trades.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Temple-bar-griffin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Temple-bar-griffin.jpg/180px-Temple-bar-griffin.jpg" width="180" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Temple-bar-griffin.jpg/270px-Temple-bar-griffin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Temple-bar-griffin.jpg/360px-Temple-bar-griffin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="733" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Temple-bar-griffin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dragon statue on the <a href="/wiki/Temple_Bar,_London" title="Temple Bar, London">Temple Bar</a> monument, which marks the boundary between the City of London and <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">City of Westminster</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Most of the wall has disappeared, but several sections remain visible. A section near the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_London" title="Museum of London">Museum of London</a> was revealed after the devastation of an air raid on 29 December 1940 at the height of the <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">Blitz</a>. Other visible sections are at <a href="/wiki/St_Alphage_London_Wall" class="mw-redirect" title="St Alphage London Wall">St Alphage</a>, and there are two sections near the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a>. The River Fleet was <a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">canalised</a> after the Great Fire of 1666 and then in stages was bricked up and has been since the 18th century one of London\'s "<a href="/wiki/Subterranean_rivers_of_London" title="Subterranean rivers of London">lost rivers or streams</a>", today underground as a <a href="/wiki/Storm_drain" title="Storm drain">storm drain</a>.\n</p><p>The boundary of the City was unchanged until minor boundary changes on 1 April 1994, when it expanded slightly to the west, north and east, taking small parcels of land from the London Boroughs of <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">Westminster</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Camden" title="London Borough of Camden">Camden</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Islington" title="London Borough of Islington">Islington</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Hackney" title="London Borough of Hackney">Hackney</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Tower_Hamlets" title="London Borough of Tower Hamlets">Tower Hamlets</a>. The main purpose of these changes was to tidy up the boundary where it had been rendered obsolete by changes in the urban landscape. In this process the City also lost small parcels of land, though there was an overall net gain (the City grew from 1.05 to 1.12 square miles). Most notably, the changes placed the (then recently developed) <a href="/wiki/Broadgate" title="Broadgate">Broadgate</a> estate entirely in the City.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Southwark" title="Southwark">Southwark</a>, to the south of the City on the other side of the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">Thames</a>, was within the City between 1550 and 1899 as the <i>Ward of <a href="/wiki/Bridge_Without" title="Bridge Without">Bridge Without</a></i>, a situation connected with the <a href="/wiki/Guildable_Manor" title="Guildable Manor">Guildable Manor</a>. The City\'s administrative responsibility there had in practice disappeared by the mid-<a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian</a> period as various aspects of metropolitan government were extended into the neighbouring areas. Today it is part of the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Southwark" title="London Borough of Southwark">London Borough of Southwark</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a> has always been outside the City and comes under the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Tower_Hamlets" title="London Borough of Tower Hamlets">London Borough of Tower Hamlets</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Arms.2C_motto_and_flag"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Arms,_motto_and_flag">Arms, motto and flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Arms, motto and flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_the_City_of_London" title="Coat of arms of the City of London">Coat of arms of the City of London</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arms_of_the_City_of_London_on_an_horse_blanket_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Arms_of_the_City_of_London_on_an_horse_blanket_2011.jpg/220px-Arms_of_the_City_of_London_on_an_horse_blanket_2011.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Arms_of_the_City_of_London_on_an_horse_blanket_2011.jpg/330px-Arms_of_the_City_of_London_on_an_horse_blanket_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Arms_of_the_City_of_London_on_an_horse_blanket_2011.jpg/440px-Arms_of_the_City_of_London_on_an_horse_blanket_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3776" data-file-height="2520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arms_of_the_City_of_London_on_an_horse_blanket_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>City of London arms on a saddle blanket, as seen outside the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Courts_of_Justice" title="Royal Courts of Justice">Royal Courts of Justice</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor%27s_Show" title="Lord Mayor&#39;s Show">Lord Mayor\'s Show</a>, 2011.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Corporation of the City of London has a full <a href="/wiki/Achievement_(heraldry)" title="Achievement (heraldry)">achievement</a> of armorial bearings consisting of a shield on which the arms are displayed, a <a href="/wiki/Crest_(heraldry)" title="Crest (heraldry)">crest</a> displayed on a helm above the shield, <a href="/wiki/Supporters" class="mw-redirect" title="Supporters">supporters</a> on either side and a motto displayed on a scroll beneath the arms.<sup id="cite_ref-briggs_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-briggs-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bening_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bening-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arms_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arms-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> is "<a href="/wiki/Time_immemorial" title="Time immemorial">anciently recorded</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Arms" title="College of Arms">College of Arms</a>. The arms consist of a silver shield bearing a red cross with a red upright sword in the first quarter. They combine the emblems of the patron saints of England and London: the <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Cross">Cross of St George</a> with the symbol of the martyrdom of <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">Saint Paul</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bening_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bening-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arms_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arms-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The sword is often erroneously supposed to commemorate the killing of <a href="/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt" title="Peasants&#39; Revolt">Peasants\' Revolt</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Wat_Tyler" title="Wat Tyler">Wat Tyler</a> by <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_London" title="Lord Mayor of London">Lord Mayor of London</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Walworth" title="William Walworth">William Walworth</a>. However the arms were in use some months before Tyler\'s death, and the tradition that Walworth\'s dagger is depicted may date from the late 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-bening_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bening-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sgiles_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sgiles-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-foxdavies_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxdavies-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-crosley_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crosley-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> motto of the City is "<i>Domine dirige nos</i>", which translates as "<i>Lord, direct (guide) us</i>". It appears to have been adopted in the 17th century, as the earliest record of it is in 1633.<sup id="cite_ref-arms_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arms-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-foxdavies_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxdavies-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Banner_of_arms" title="Banner of arms">banner of the arms</a> (the design on the shield) is flown as a <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_City_of_London" title="Flag of the City of London">flag</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The City is England\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="List of ceremonial counties of England">smallest ceremonial county</a> by area and population, and the fourth most densely populated. Of the <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_England" title="Districts of England">326 English districts</a>, it is the second smallest <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_population" title="List of English districts by population">by population</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>, and the smallest <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_area" title="List of English districts by area">by area</a>. It is also <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_United_Kingdom#England" title="List of cities in the United Kingdom">the smallest English</a> <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> by population (and in Britain, only two cities in Wales are smaller), and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_smallest_cities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of smallest cities in the United Kingdom">smallest in the UK by area</a>.\n</p><p>The elevation of the City ranges from sea level at the Thames to 21.6 metres (71&#160;ft) at the junction of High Holborn and Chancery Lane.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Two small but notable hills are within the historic core, <a href="/wiki/Ludgate_Hill" title="Ludgate Hill">Ludgate Hill</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/Cornhill,_London" title="Cornhill, London">Cornhill</a> to the east. Between them ran the <a href="/wiki/Walbrook" title="Walbrook">Walbrook</a>, one of the many <a href="/wiki/Subterranean_rivers_of_London" title="Subterranean rivers of London">"lost" rivers or streams of London</a> (another is the <a href="/wiki/River_Fleet" title="River Fleet">Fleet</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boundary">Boundary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Boundary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_map_01.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/City_of_London_map_01.svg/220px-City_of_London_map_01.svg.png" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/City_of_London_map_01.svg/330px-City_of_London_map_01.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/City_of_London_map_01.svg/440px-City_of_London_map_01.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="4778" data-file-height="3708" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_map_01.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Borders of the City of London, showing surrounding <a href="/wiki/London_borough" class="mw-redirect" title="London borough">London boroughs</a> and the pre-1994 boundary (where changed) in red. The area covered by the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Temple" title="Inner Temple">Inner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Temple" title="Middle Temple">Middle Temple</a> is marked.</div></div></div>\n<p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mapping.cityoflondon.gov.uk/geocortex/mapping/?viewer=compass">Official boundary map, with wards.</a>\n</p><p>Beginning in the west, where the City borders Westminster, the boundary crosses the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Embankment" title="Victoria Embankment">Victoria Embankment</a> from the Thames, passes to the west of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Temple" title="Middle Temple">Middle Temple</a>, then turns for a short distance along <a href="/wiki/Strand,_London" title="Strand, London">Strand</a> and then north up <a href="/wiki/Chancery_Lane" title="Chancery Lane">Chancery Lane</a>, where it borders Camden. It turns east along <a href="/wiki/Holborn" title="Holborn">Holborn</a> to Holborn Circus, and then goes north east to <a href="/wiki/Charterhouse_Street" title="Charterhouse Street">Charterhouse Street</a>. As it crosses <a href="/wiki/Farringdon_Road" title="Farringdon Road">Farringdon Road</a> it becomes the boundary with Islington. It continues to <a href="/wiki/Aldersgate" title="Aldersgate">Aldersgate</a>, goes north, and turns east into some back streets soon after Aldersgate becomes <a href="/wiki/Goswell_Road" title="Goswell Road">Goswell Road</a>, since 1994 embracing all of the Corporation\'s Golden Lane Estate. Here, at Baltic Street West, is the most northerly extent. The boundary includes all of the <a href="/wiki/Barbican_Estate" title="Barbican Estate">Barbican Estate</a> and continues east along Ropemaker Street and its continuation on the other side of <a href="/wiki/Moorgate" title="Moorgate">Moorgate</a>, becomes South Place. It goes north, reaching the border with Hackney, then east, north, east on back streets, with Worship Street forming a northern boundary, so as to include the <a href="/wiki/Broadgate" title="Broadgate">Broadgate</a> estate. The boundary then turns south at <a href="/wiki/Norton_Folgate" title="Norton Folgate">Norton Folgate</a> and becomes the border with <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Tower_Hamlets" title="London Borough of Tower Hamlets">Tower Hamlets</a>. It continues south into <a href="/wiki/Bishopsgate" title="Bishopsgate">Bishopsgate</a>, and takes some backstreets to Middlesex Street (<a href="/wiki/Petticoat_Lane" class="mw-redirect" title="Petticoat Lane">Petticoat Lane</a>) where it continues south-east then south. It then turns south-west, crossing the <a href="/wiki/Minories" title="Minories">Minories</a> so as to exclude the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a>, and then reaches the river. It then runs up the centre of the Thames, with the exception that <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_Bridge" title="Blackfriars Bridge">Blackfriars Bridge</a> falls within the City; the City controls <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge" title="London Bridge">London Bridge</a> (as part of <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(ward)" title="Bridge (ward)">Bridge</a> ward) but only half of the river underneath it, a feature which is unique in British local administration.\n</p><p>The boundaries are marked by black bollards bearing the City\'s emblem, and by <a href="/wiki/Dragon_boundary_mark" title="Dragon boundary mark">dragon boundary marks</a> at major entrances, such as Holborn. A more substantial monument marks the boundary at <a href="/wiki/Temple_Bar,_London" title="Temple Bar, London">Temple Bar</a> on Fleet Street.\n</p><p>In some places the financial district extends slightly beyond the boundaries, notably to the north and east, into the London Boroughs of Tower Hamlets, Hackney and Islington, and informally these locations are seen as part of the "Square Mile". Since the 1990s the eastern fringe, extending into Hackney and Tower Hamlets, has increasingly been a focus for large office developments due to the availability of large sites compared to within the City.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gardens_and_public_art">Gardens and public art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Gardens and public art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_public_art_in_the_City_of_London" title="List of public art in the City of London">List of public art in the City of London</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Finsbury_Circus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Finsbury_Circus.jpg/220px-Finsbury_Circus.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Finsbury_Circus.jpg/330px-Finsbury_Circus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Finsbury_Circus.jpg/440px-Finsbury_Circus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3247" data-file-height="2421" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Finsbury_Circus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Finsbury_Circus" title="Finsbury Circus">Finsbury Circus</a>, the largest public open space, seen from <a href="/wiki/Tower_42" title="Tower 42">Tower 42</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The City has no sizeable parks within its boundary, but does have a network of a large number of gardens and small open spaces, many of them maintained by the Corporation. These range from formal gardens such as the one in <a href="/wiki/Finsbury_Circus" title="Finsbury Circus">Finsbury Circus</a>, containing a <a href="/wiki/Bowling_green" title="Bowling green">bowling green</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bandstand" title="Bandstand">bandstand</a>, to churchyards such as <a href="/wiki/St_Olave_Hart_Street" title="St Olave Hart Street">St Olave Hart Street</a>, to water features and artwork in courtyards and pedestrianised lanes.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gardens include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Barber-Surgeon\'s Hall Garden, <a href="/wiki/London_Wall" title="London Wall">London Wall</a></li>\n<li>Cleary Garden, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria_Street,_London" title="Queen Victoria Street, London">Queen Victoria Street</a><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Finsbury_Circus" title="Finsbury Circus">Finsbury Circus</a>, Blomfield Street/London Wall/<a href="/wiki/Moorgate" title="Moorgate">Moorgate</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jubilee_Garden" title="Jubilee Garden">Jubilee Garden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houndsditch" title="Houndsditch">Houndsditch</a></li>\n<li>Portsoken Street Garden, Portsoken Street/Goodman\'s Yard</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Postman%27s_Park" title="Postman&#39;s Park">Postman\'s Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Little_Britain,_London" title="Little Britain, London">Little Britain</a></li>\n<li>Seething Lane Garden, Seething Lane</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St_Dunstan-in-the-East" title="St Dunstan-in-the-East">St Dunstan-in-the-East</a>, St Dunstan\'s Hill</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St_Mary_Aldermanbury" title="St Mary Aldermanbury">St Mary Aldermanbury</a>, Aldermanbury</li>\n<li>St Olave Hart Street churchyard, Seething Lane</li>\n<li>St Paul\'s churchyard, <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul&#39;s Cathedral">St Paul\'s Cathedral</a></li>\n<li>West Smithfield Garden, <a href="/wiki/West_Smithfield" class="mw-redirect" title="West Smithfield">West Smithfield</a></li>\n<li>Whittington Gardens, College Street</li></ul>\n<p>There are a number of private gardens and open spaces, often within courtyards of the larger commercial developments. Two of the largest are those of the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Temple" title="Inner Temple">Inner Temple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Temple" title="Middle Temple">Middle Temple</a> Inns of Court, in the far southwest.\n</p><p>The Thames and its riverside walks are increasingly being valued as open space and in recent years efforts have been made to increase the ability for pedestrians to access and walk along the river.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The nearest weather station has historically been the London Weather Centre at <a href="/wiki/Kingsway,_London" title="Kingsway, London">Kingsway</a>/ <a href="/wiki/Holborn" title="Holborn">Holborn</a>, although observations ceased in 2010. Now St. James Park provides the nearest official readings.\n</p><p>The City has an <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime Climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen</a> "Cfb") modified by the <a href="/wiki/Urban_Heat_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban Heat Island">Urban Heat Island</a> in the centre of London. This generally causes higher night-time minima than outlying areas. For example, the August mean minimum<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> of 14.7&#160;\xc2\xb0C (58.5&#160;\xc2\xb0F) compares to a figure of 13.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (55.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F) for Greenwich<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and Heathrow<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> whereas is 11.6&#160;\xc2\xb0C (52.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F) at Wisley<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> in the middle of several square miles of <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Green_Belt" title="Metropolitan Green Belt">Metropolitan Green Belt</a>. All figures refer to the observation period 1971\xe2\x80\x932000.\n</p><p>Accordingly, the weather station holds the record for the UK\'s warmest overnight minimum temperature, 24.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (75.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F), recorded on 4 August 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The maximum is 37.6&#160;\xc2\xb0C (99.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F), set on 10 August 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The absolute minimum<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> for the weather station is a mere \xe2\x88\x928.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (17.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F), compared to readings around \xe2\x88\x9215.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (5.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F) towards the edges of London. Unusually, this temperature was during a windy and snowy cold spell (mid-January 1987), rather than a cold clear night\xe2\x80\x94cold air drainage is arrested due to the vast urban area surrounding the city.\n</p><p>The station holds the record for the highest British mean monthly temperature,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> 24.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (76.1&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (mean maximum 29.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (84.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F), mean minimum 19.7&#160;\xc2\xb0C (67.5&#160;\xc2\xb0F) during July 2006). However, in terms of daytime maximum temperatures, Cambridge NIAB<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and Botanical Gardens<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> with a mean maximum of 29.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (84.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and Heathrow<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> with 29.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (84.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F) all exceeded this.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data for London Weather Centre 1971\xe2\x80\x932000, 43&#160;m asl\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Domine_Dirige_Nos_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1111983.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Domine_Dirige_Nos_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1111983.jpg/200px-Domine_Dirige_Nos_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1111983.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Domine_Dirige_Nos_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1111983.jpg/300px-Domine_Dirige_Nos_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1111983.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Domine_Dirige_Nos_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1111983.jpg/400px-Domine_Dirige_Nos_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1111983.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Domine_Dirige_Nos_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1111983.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>City of London coat of arms on the street</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police_and_security">Police and security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Police and security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_Police_Mitsubishi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/City_of_London_Police_Mitsubishi.jpg/200px-City_of_London_Police_Mitsubishi.jpg" width="200" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/City_of_London_Police_Mitsubishi.jpg/300px-City_of_London_Police_Mitsubishi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/City_of_London_Police_Mitsubishi.jpg/400px-City_of_London_Police_Mitsubishi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5194" data-file-height="3378" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_Police_Mitsubishi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A City of London Police vehicle on <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_Bridge" title="Blackfriars Bridge">Blackfriars Bridge</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The City is a <a href="/wiki/Police_area" title="Police area">police area</a> and has its own <a href="/wiki/Territorial_police_force" title="Territorial police force">police force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Police" title="City of London Police">City of London Police</a>, separate from the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police_Service" title="Metropolitan Police Service">Metropolitan Police Service</a> covering the remainder of Greater London. The City Police have three police stations, at Snow Hill, <a href="/wiki/Wood_Street,_London" title="Wood Street, London">Wood Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bishopsgate" title="Bishopsgate">Bishopsgate</a>, and an administrative headquarters at Guildhall Yard East.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The force comprises 813 police officers, 85 <a href="/wiki/Special_Constables" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Constables">Special Constables</a> and 48 <a href="/wiki/Police_Community_Support_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Police Community Support Officer">PCSOs</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It is the smallest territorial police force in <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>, in both geographic area and the number of police officers.\n</p><p>Where the majority of British police forces have silver-coloured badges, those of the City of London Police are black and gold featuring the City crest. The force has unique red and white chequered cap bands and red and white striped duty arm bands on the sleeve of the tunics of constables and sergeants (red and white being the colours of the City), which in most other British police forces are black and white. City police sergeants and constables wear crested <a href="/wiki/Custodian_helmet" title="Custodian helmet">helmets</a> whilst on foot patrol. These helmets do not feature either <a href="/wiki/St_Edward%27s_Crown" title="St Edward&#39;s Crown">St Edward\'s Crown</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Star" class="mw-redirect" title="Brunswick Star">Brunswick Star</a>, which are used on most other police helmets in <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>.\n</p><p>The City\'s position as the United Kingdom\'s financial centre and a critical part of the country\'s economy, contributing about 2.5% of the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross national product">gross national product</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> has resulted in it becoming a target for political violence. The <a href="/wiki/Provisional_IRA" class="mw-redirect" title="Provisional IRA">Provisional IRA</a> exploded several <a href="/wiki/Bomb" title="Bomb">bombs</a> in the early 1990s, including the <a href="/wiki/1993_Bishopsgate_bombing" title="1993 Bishopsgate bombing">1993 Bishopsgate bombing</a>.\n</p><p>The area is also spoken of as a possible target for <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a>. For instance, when in May 2004 the BBC\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Panorama_(TV_series)" title="Panorama (TV series)">Panorama</a></i> programme examined the preparedness of Britain\'s emergency services for a terrorist attack on the scale of <a href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="September 11, 2001 attacks">September 11, 2001 attacks</a>, they simulated a chemical explosion on <a href="/wiki/Bishopsgate" title="Bishopsgate">Bishopsgate</a> in the east of the City.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_steel_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ring of steel (London)">"Ring of Steel"</a> is a particularly notable measure, established in the wake of the IRA bombings, that has been taken against terrorist threats.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fire_brigade">Fire brigade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fire brigade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/London_Fire_Brigade" title="London Fire Brigade">London Fire Brigade</a></div>\n<p>The City has fire risks in many historic buildings, including <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul&#39;s Cathedral">St Paul\'s Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Bailey" title="Old Bailey">Old Bailey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mansion_House,_London" title="Mansion House, London">Mansion House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smithfield_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="Smithfield Market">Smithfield Market</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Guildhall,_London" title="Guildhall, London">Guildhall</a>, and also in numerous high-rise buildings. There is one London Fire Brigade station in the City, at <a href="/wiki/Dowgate" title="Dowgate">Dowgate</a>, with one <a href="/wiki/Fire_appliances_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Fire appliances in the United Kingdom">pumping appliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-zlqtbi_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zlqtbi-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The City relies upon stations in the surrounding London boroughs to support it at some incidents. The first fire engine is in attendance in roughly five minutes on average, the second when required in a little over five and a half minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-zlqtbi_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zlqtbi-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> There were 1,814 incidents attended in the City in 2006/2007\xe2\x80\x94the lowest in Greater London. No-one died in an event arising from a fire in the four years prior to 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-zlqtbi_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zlqtbi-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="toccolours" #bbbbbb">\xe2\x88\x9230.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"> <a href="/wiki/Census_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Census in the United Kingdom">1951</a> </th><td #bbbbbb">\xe2\x88\x9216.1%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"> <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">2001</a> </th><td
