style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Sources: <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a> recorded the population in 2011 as 7,375;<sup id="cite_ref-2010pop_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010pop-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> slightly higher than in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">last census</a>, 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-census_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and estimates the population as at mid-2016 to be 9,401. At the 2001 census the ethnic composition was 84.6% <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a>, 6.8% <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">South Asian</a>, 2.6% <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Black</a>, 2.3% <a href="/wiki/British_Mixed-Race" class="mw-redirect" title="British Mixed-Race">Mixed</a>, 2.0% <a href="/wiki/British_Chinese" title="British Chinese">Chinese</a> and 1.7% were listed as "<a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Ethnic groups in the United Kingdom">other</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-census_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> To the right is a table showing the change in population since 1801, based on <a href="/wiki/Census_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Census in the United Kingdom">decadal censuses</a>. The first half of the 19th century shows a population of between 120,000\xe2\x80\x93140,000, decreasing dramatically from 1851 to 1991, with a small increase between 1991 and 2001. The only notable boundary change since the first census in 1801 occurred in 1994.\n</p><p>The City\'s full-time working residents have much higher gross weekly pay than in London and Great Britain (England, Wales and Scotland): \xc2\xa3773.30 compared to \xc2\xa3598.60 and \xc2\xa3491.00 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-nomis_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nomis-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> There is a large inequality of income between genders (\xc2\xa31,085.90 in men compared to \xc2\xa3653.50 in women), though this can be explained by job type and length of employment respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-nomis_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nomis-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The 2001 Census showed the City as a unique district amongst 376 districts surveyed in <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts" title="List of English districts">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Wales" title="Districts of Wales">Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-census_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The City had the highest proportional population increase, one-person households, people with qualifications at degree level or higher and the highest indications of overcrowding.<sup id="cite_ref-census_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> It recorded the lowest proportion of households with cars or vans, people who travel to work by car, married couple households and the lowest average household size: just 1.58 people.<sup id="cite_ref-census_63-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> It also ranked highest within the Greater London area for the percentage of people with no religion and people who are employed.<sup id="cite_ref-census_63-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_London" title="Economy of London">Economy of London</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Banco_de_Inglaterra,_Londres,_Inglaterra,_2014-08-11,_DD_141.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Banco_de_Inglaterra%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_141.JPG/220px-Banco_de_Inglaterra%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_141.JPG" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Banco_de_Inglaterra%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_141.JPG/330px-Banco_de_Inglaterra%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_141.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Banco_de_Inglaterra%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_141.JPG/440px-Banco_de_Inglaterra%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_141.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4978" data-file-height="3548" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Banco_de_Inglaterra,_Londres,_Inglaterra,_2014-08-11,_DD_141.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Threadneedle_Street" title="Threadneedle Street">Threadneedle Street</a>, is the central bank of the United Kingdom.</div></div></div>\n<p>The City vies with New York City as the <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial capital</a> of the world; many banking and insurance institutions have their headquarters there. The <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> (<a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">shares</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a>), <a href="/wiki/Lloyd%27s_of_London" title="Lloyd&#39;s of London">Lloyd\'s of London</a> (insurance) and the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> are all based in the City. Over 500 banks have offices in the City, and the City is an established leader in trading in <a href="/wiki/Eurobond" title="Eurobond">Eurobonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a>, energy <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">futures</a> and global insurance. The <a href="/wiki/Alternative_Investment_Market" title="Alternative Investment Market">Alternative Investment Market</a>, a market for trades in <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">equities</a> of smaller firms, is a recent development. In 2009, the City of London accounted for 2.4% of UK GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-citylondon_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citylondon-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>London is the world\'s greatest <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange market</a>, with much of the trade conducted in the City of London. Of the $3.98&#160;trillion daily global turnover, as measured in 2009, trading in London accounted for around $1.85&#160;trillion, or 46.7% of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-citylondon_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citylondon-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">pound sterling</a>, the currency of the United Kingdom, is globally the fourth most traded currency and the third most held <a href="/wiki/Reserve_currency" title="Reserve currency">reserve currency</a>.\n</p><p>Since 1991 <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf" title="Canary Wharf">Canary Wharf</a>, a few miles east of the City in Tower Hamlets, has become another centre for London\'s financial services industry which houses many banks and other institutions formerly located in the Square Mile. Although growth has continued in both locations, and there have been relocations in both directions, the Corporation has come to realise that its planning policies may have been causing financial firms to choose Canary Wharf as a location.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Headquarters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paternoster_Square.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Paternoster_Square.jpg/220px-Paternoster_Square.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Paternoster_Square.jpg/330px-Paternoster_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Paternoster_Square.jpg/440px-Paternoster_Square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paternoster_Square.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Paternoster_Square" title="Paternoster Square">Paternoster Square</a>, since 2004 the home of the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Many major global companies have their headquarters in the City, including <a href="/wiki/Aviva" title="Aviva">Aviva</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lloyds_Banking_Group" title="Lloyds Banking Group">Lloyds Banking Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Old_Mutual" title="Old Mutual">Old Mutual</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prudential_plc" title="Prudential plc">Prudential</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Schroders_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Schroders plc">Schroders</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chartered_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Chartered Bank">Standard Chartered</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Unilever_PLC" class="mw-redirect" title="Unilever PLC">Unilever</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A number of the world\'s largest law firms are headquartered in the City, including four of the "<a href="/wiki/Magic_Circle_(law_firms)" title="Magic Circle (law firms)">Magic Circle</a>" law firms (<a href="/wiki/Allen_%26_Overy" title="Allen &amp; Overy">Allen &amp; Overy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freshfields_Bruckhaus_Deringer" title="Freshfields Bruckhaus Deringer">Freshfields Bruckhaus Deringer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linklaters" title="Linklaters">Linklaters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slaughter_%26_May" class="mw-redirect" title="Slaughter &amp; May">Slaughter &amp; May</a>), as well as other firms such as <a href="/wiki/DLA_Piper" title="DLA Piper">DLA Piper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eversheds_Sutherland" title="Eversheds Sutherland">Eversheds Sutherland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Smith_Freehills" title="Herbert Smith Freehills">Herbert Smith Freehills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hogan_Lovells" title="Hogan Lovells">Hogan Lovells</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sectors">Other sectors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other sectors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbican_Centre_City_of_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Barbican_Centre_City_of_London.jpg/220px-Barbican_Centre_City_of_London.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Barbican_Centre_City_of_London.jpg/330px-Barbican_Centre_City_of_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Barbican_Centre_City_of_London.jpg/440px-Barbican_Centre_City_of_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbican_Centre_City_of_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Barbican Centre</div></div></div>\n<p>Whilst the financial sector, and related businesses and institutions, continue to dominate, the economy is not limited to that sector. The legal profession has a strong presence, especially in the west and north (i.e., towards the <a href="/wiki/Inns_of_Court" title="Inns of Court">Inns of Court</a>). Retail businesses were once important, but have gradually moved to the <a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End of London</a>, though it is now Corporation policy to encourage retailing in some locations, for example at <a href="/wiki/Cheapside" title="Cheapside">Cheapside</a> near St Paul\'s. The City has a number of visitor attractions, mainly based on its historic heritage as well as the <a href="/wiki/Barbican_Centre" title="Barbican Centre">Barbican Centre</a> and adjacent <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_London" title="Museum of London">Museum of London</a>, though tourism is not at present a major contributor to the City\'s economy or character. The City has many pubs, bars and restaurants, and the "night-time" economy does feature in the <a href="/wiki/Bishopsgate" title="Bishopsgate">Bishopsgate</a> area, towards <a href="/wiki/Shoreditch" title="Shoreditch">Shoreditch</a>. The meat market <a href="/wiki/Smithfield_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="Smithfield Market">at Smithfield</a>, wholly within the City, continues to be one of London\'s main markets (the only one remaining in central London) and the country\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Butcher" title="Butcher">meat market</a>. In the east is <a href="/wiki/Leadenhall_Market" title="Leadenhall Market">Leadenhall Market</a>, a fresh food market that is also a visitor attraction.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retail_and_residential">Retail and residential</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Retail and residential">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The trend for purely office development is beginning to reverse as the Corporation encourages residential use, albeit with development occurring when it arises on windfall sites. The City has a target of 90 additional dwellings per year.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Some of the extra accommodation is in small pre-<a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed buildings</a>, which are not suitable for occupation by the large companies which now provide much of the City\'s employment. Recent residential developments include "the Heron", a high-rise residential building on the Milton Court site adjacent to the Barbican, and the <a href="/wiki/Heron_Tower#Heron_Plaza" title="Heron Tower">Heron Plaza</a> development on Bishopsgate is also expected to include residential parts.\n</p><p>Since the 1990s, the City has diversified away from near exclusive office use in other ways. For example, several hotels and the first <a href="/wiki/Department_store" title="Department store">department store</a> opened in the 2000s. A shopping centre was more recently opened at <a href="/wiki/One_New_Change" title="One New Change">One New Change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheapside" title="Cheapside">Cheapside</a> (near St Paul\'s Cathedral) in October 2010, which is open seven days a week. However, large sections remain quiet at weekends, especially in the eastern section, and it is quite common to find shops, <a href="/wiki/Public_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Public house">pubs</a> and cafes closed on these days.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_buildings">Historical buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Historical buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Fire, bombing and post-<a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> redevelopment has meant that the City, despite its history, has relatively few intact notable historic structures. They include the <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Great_Fire_of_London" title="Monument to the Great Fire of London">Monument to the Great Fire of London</a> ("the Monument"), <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul&#39;s Cathedral">St Paul\'s Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guildhall,_London" title="Guildhall, London">the Guildhall</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Exchange,_London" title="Royal Exchange, London">Royal Exchange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Johnson%27s_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Dr. Johnson&#39;s House">Dr. Johnson\'s House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mansion_House,_London" title="Mansion House, London">Mansion House</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Category:Churches_in_the_City_of_London" title="Category:Churches in the City of London">great many churches</a>, many designed by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Christopher_Wren" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Christopher Wren">Sir Christopher Wren</a>, who also designed St Paul\'s. <a href="/wiki/2_King%27s_Bench_Walk" title="2 King&#39;s Bench Walk">2 King\'s Bench Walk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Henry%27s_Room" title="Prince Henry&#39;s Room">Prince Henry\'s Room</a> are notable historic survivors of heavy bombing of <a href="/wiki/Temple,_London" title="Temple, London">the Temple</a> area, which has largely been rebuilt to its historic form. Another example of a bomb-damaged place having been restored is <a href="/wiki/Staple_Inn" title="Staple Inn">Staple Inn</a> on Holborn. A few small sections of the Roman <a href="/wiki/London_Wall" title="London Wall">London Wall</a> exist, for example near the Tower of London and in the Barbican area. Among the twentieth-century <a href="/wiki/Listed_buildings" class="mw-redirect" title="Listed buildings">listed buildings</a> are <a href="/wiki/Bracken_House,_London" title="Bracken House, London">Bracken House</a>, the first post World War II buildings in the country to be given statutory protection, and the whole of the <a href="/wiki/Barbican_Estate" title="Barbican Estate">Barbican</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Lane_Estate" title="Golden Lane Estate">Golden Lane Estate</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a> is not in the City, but is a notable visitor attraction which brings tourists to the southeast of the City. Other landmark buildings with historical significance include the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bailey" title="Old Bailey">Old Bailey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Custom_House,_City_of_London" title="Custom House, City of London">Custom House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smithfield,_London" title="Smithfield, London">Smithfield Market</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leadenhall_Market" title="Leadenhall Market">Leadenhall Market</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Bartholomew%27s_Hospital" title="St Bartholomew&#39;s Hospital">St Bartholomew\'s Hospital</a>. Noteworthy contemporary buildings include a number of modern high-rise buildings (see section below) as well as the <a href="/wiki/Lloyd%27s_building" title="Lloyd&#39;s building">Lloyd\'s building</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Exchange_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Royal_Exchange_Panorama.jpg/500px-Royal_Exchange_Panorama.jpg" width="500" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Royal_Exchange_Panorama.jpg/750px-Royal_Exchange_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Royal_Exchange_Panorama.jpg/1000px-Royal_Exchange_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10288" data-file-height="4784" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Exchange_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Bank of England (left) and the Royal Exchange (centre) are two of the many significant buildings in the City of London.</div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Skyscrapers_and_tall_buildings">Skyscrapers and tall buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Skyscrapers and tall buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_and_structures_in_London" title="List of tallest buildings and structures in London">List of tallest buildings and structures in London</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2016-02_City_of_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/2016-02_City_of_London.jpg/220px-2016-02_City_of_London.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/2016-02_City_of_London.jpg/330px-2016-02_City_of_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/2016-02_City_of_London.jpg/440px-2016-02_City_of_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2016-02_City_of_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The City skyline in February 2016, including <a href="/wiki/20_Fenchurch_Street" title="20 Fenchurch Street">20 Fenchurch Street</a> (left), the <a href="/wiki/122_Leadenhall_Street" title="122 Leadenhall Street">Leadenhall Building</a> (centre) and <a href="/wiki/30_St_Mary_Axe" title="30 St Mary Axe">30 St Mary Axe</a> (right)</div></div></div>\n<dl><dt>Completed</dt></dl>\n<p>A growing number of tall buildings and skyscrapers are principally used by the financial sector. Almost all are situated in the eastern side around <a href="/wiki/Bishopsgate" title="Bishopsgate">Bishopsgate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leadenhall_Street" title="Leadenhall Street">Leadenhall Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fenchurch_Street" title="Fenchurch Street">Fenchurch Street</a>, in the financial core of the City. In the north there is a smaller cluster comprising the <a href="/wiki/Barbican_Estate" title="Barbican Estate">Barbican Estate</a>\'s three tall residential towers and the commercial <a href="/wiki/CityPoint" title="CityPoint">CityPoint</a> tower. In 2007, the 100&#160;m (328&#160;ft) tall <a href="/wiki/Drapers%27_Gardens" title="Drapers&#39; Gardens">Drapers\' Gardens</a> building was demolished and replaced by a shorter tower.\n</p><p>The City\'s buildings of more than 100&#160;m (328&#160;ft) in height are:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="border:#999; id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_London" title="Transport in London">Transport in London</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_station_MMB_07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_station_MMB_07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>London Underground <a href="/wiki/Roundel" title="Roundel">roundel</a> (flanked by City dragons) at <a href="/wiki/Bank%E2%80%93Monument_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank\xe2\x80\x93Monument station">Bank</a> station.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Orilla_Norte_del_T%C3%A1mesis_desde_Tate_Modern%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_123.JPG/330px-Orilla_Norte_del_T%C3%A1mesis_desde_Tate_Modern%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_123.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Orilla_Norte_del_T%C3%A1mesis_desde_Tate_Modern%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_123.JPG/440px-Orilla_Norte_del_T%C3%A1mesis_desde_Tate_Modern%2C_Londres%2C_Inglaterra%2C_2014-08-11%2C_DD_123.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5454" data-file-height="3113" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Orilla_Norte_del_T%C3%A1mesis_desde_Tate_Modern,_Londres,_Inglaterra,_2014-08-11,_DD_123.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Bridge_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Bridge (London)">Millennium Bridge</a>, looking north towards St Paul\'s Cathedral and the City.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Seven of the eleven <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> lines run through the City, serving eleven <a href="/wiki/List_of_London_Underground_stations" title="List of London Underground stations">stations</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Light_Railway" title="Docklands Light Railway">Docklands Light Railway</a> (DLR) has two <a href="/wiki/List_of_Docklands_Light_Railway_stations" title="List of Docklands Light Railway stations">stations</a> within the City: <a href="/wiki/Bank_Underground_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank Underground station">Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tower_Gateway_DLR_station" title="Tower Gateway DLR station">Tower Gateway</a>.\n</p><p>Three longer-distance rail termini are in the City: <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street</a> (services primarily to Essex and East Anglia including <a href="/wiki/Southend_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Southend Airport">Southend Airport</a>), <a href="/wiki/Fenchurch_Street_railway_station" title="Fenchurch Street railway station">Fenchurch Street</a> (services to East London and South Essex) and <a href="/wiki/Cannon_Street_station" title="Cannon Street station">Cannon Street</a> (services to the South).\n</p><p>Moorgate is the terminus for suburban services from <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a>, and two through-routes operate mostly underground along the main axes:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>North to South:</i> <a href="/wiki/City_Thameslink_railway_station" title="City Thameslink railway station">City Thameslink</a> (north) and <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_station" title="Blackfriars station">Blackfriars</a> (south) are both on the <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_(route)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thameslink (route)">Thameslink line</a> with trains running from <a href="/wiki/Bedford" title="Bedford">Bedford</a> to <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">Brighton</a>, serving <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_International" class="mw-redirect" title="St Pancras International">St Pancras International</a> <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> terminus, <a href="/wiki/London_Gatwick_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Gatwick Airport">Gatwick</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">Luton</a> airports.</li>\n<li><i>East to West:</i> <a href="/wiki/Crossrail" title="Crossrail">Crossrail</a> is under construction, but upon completion will serve <a href="/wiki/Farringdon_station" title="Farringdon station">Farringdon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moorgate_station" title="Moorgate station">Moorgate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street stations</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Northern_line" title="Northern line">Northern line</a> connects to two other main railway termini, <a href="/wiki/London_Euston_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Euston station">Euston</a>) and (<a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_station" title="London Waterloo station">Waterloo</a>)); the latter has a direct connection to the City via the <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_and_City_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Waterloo and City Line">Waterloo and City Line</a>.\n</p><p>The City is in <a href="/wiki/Travelcard_Zone_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Travelcard Zone 1">Travelcard Zone 1</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Space_taken_vs_numbers_in_City_of_London_(transport).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Space_taken_vs_numbers_in_City_of_London_%28transport%29.png/220px-Space_taken_vs_numbers_in_City_of_London_%28transport%29.png" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Space_taken_vs_numbers_in_City_of_London_%28transport%29.png/330px-Space_taken_vs_numbers_in_City_of_London_%28transport%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Space_taken_vs_numbers_in_City_of_London_%28transport%29.png/440px-Space_taken_vs_numbers_in_City_of_London_%28transport%29.png 2x" data-file-width="773" data-file-height="365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Space_taken_vs_numbers_in_City_of_London_(transport).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Space taken vs numbers in City of London (transport)</div></div></div>\n<p>The national <a href="/wiki/A1_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A1 road (Great Britain)">A1</a>, <a href="/wiki/A10_road_(England)" title="A10 road (England)">A10</a> <a href="/wiki/A3_road" title="A3 road">A3</a>, <a href="/wiki/A4_road_(England)" title="A4 road (England)">A4</a>, and <a href="/wiki/A40_road" title="A40 road">A40 road</a> routes begin in the City. The City is in the <a href="/wiki/London_congestion_charge" title="London congestion charge">London congestion charge</a> zone, with the small exception on the eastern boundary of the sections of the A1210/A1211 that are part of the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Ring_Road,_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Inner Ring Road, London">inner ring road</a>. The following bridges, listed west to east (downstream), cross the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a>: <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_Bridge" title="Blackfriars Bridge">Blackfriars Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_Railway_Bridge" title="Blackfriars Railway Bridge">Blackfriars Railway Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Bridge_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Bridge (London)">Millennium Bridge</a> (footbridge), <a href="/wiki/Southwark_Bridge" title="Southwark Bridge">Southwark Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cannon_Street_Railway_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Cannon Street Railway Bridge">Cannon Street Railway Bridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge" title="London Bridge">London Bridge</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tower_Bridge" title="Tower Bridge">Tower Bridge</a> is not in the City. The City, like most of central London, is well <a href="/wiki/Buses_in_London" title="Buses in London">served by buses</a>, including night buses. Two bus stations are in the City, at <a href="/wiki/Aldgate_bus_station" title="Aldgate bus station">Aldgate</a> on the eastern boundary with Tower Hamlets, and at <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_bus_station" title="Liverpool Street bus station">Liverpool Street</a> by the railway station. There are approximately 28 <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Cycle_Hire" class="mw-redirect" title="Barclays Cycle Hire">Barclays Cycle Hire</a> docking stations in the City.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> A number of existing and proposed cycle routes criss-cross the City, as part of the <a href="/wiki/London_Cycle_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="London Cycle Network">London Cycle Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="River">River</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: River">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>One <a href="/wiki/London_River_Services" title="London River Services">London River Services</a> pier is on the Thames in the City, <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_Millennium_Pier" title="Blackfriars Millennium Pier">Blackfriars Millennium Pier</a>, though the <a href="/wiki/Tower_Millennium_Pier" title="Tower Millennium Pier">Tower Millennium Pier</a> lies adjacent to the boundary near the Tower of London. One of the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_London" title="Port of London">Port of London</a>\'s 25 <a href="/wiki/Safeguarded_wharf" title="Safeguarded wharf">safeguarded wharves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walbrook_Wharf" title="Walbrook Wharf">Walbrook Wharf</a>, is adjacent to Cannon Street station, and is used by the Corporation to transfer waste via the river. Swan Lane Pier, just upstream of London Bridge, is proposed to be replaced and upgraded for regular passenger services, planned to take place in 2012\xe2\x80\x932015. Before then, Tower Pier is to be extended.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is a public riverside walk along the river bank, opened in stages over recent years. The only section not running along the river is a short stretch at <a href="/wiki/Queenhithe" title="Queenhithe">Queenhithe</a>. The walk along Walbrook Wharf is closed to pedestrians when waste is being transferred onto barges.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Travel_to_work_.28by_residents.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Travel_to_work_(by_residents)">Travel to work (by residents)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Travel to work (by residents)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to a survey conducted in March 2011, the methods by which employed residents 16-74 get to work varied widely: 48.4% go on foot; 19.5% via light rail, (i.e. <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">the Underground</a>, <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Light_Railway" title="Docklands Light Railway">DLR</a>, etc.); 9.2% work mainly from home; 5.8% take the train; 5.6% travel by bus, minibus, or coach; and 5.3% go by bicycle; with just 3.4% commuting by car or van, as driver or passenger.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KCLMaughanLibrary2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/KCLMaughanLibrary2.jpg/220px-KCLMaughanLibrary2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/KCLMaughanLibrary2.jpg/330px-KCLMaughanLibrary2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/KCLMaughanLibrary2.jpg/440px-KCLMaughanLibrary2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KCLMaughanLibrary2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Maughan_Library" title="Maughan Library">Maughan Library</a>, <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King&#39;s College London">King\'s College London</a>, located on <a href="/wiki/Chancery_Lane" title="Chancery Lane">Chancery Lane</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The City has only one directly maintained primary school, Sir John Cass\'s Foundation Primary School at <a href="/wiki/Aldgate" title="Aldgate">Aldgate</a><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> (ages 4 to 11). It is a Voluntary-Aided (VA) <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> school, maintained by the Education Service of the City of London.\n</p><p>City residents send their children to schools in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Local_Education_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Local Education Authority">Local Education Authorities</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Islington" title="London Borough of Islington">Islington</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Tower_Hamlets" title="London Borough of Tower Hamlets">Tower Hamlets</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">Westminster</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Southwark" title="London Borough of Southwark">Southwark</a>.\n</p><p>The City controls three independent schools, <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_School" title="City of London School">City of London School</a> (a boys\' school) and <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_School_for_Girls" title="City of London School for Girls">City of London School for Girls</a> in the City, and the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Freemen%27s_School" title="City of London Freemen&#39;s School">City of London Freemen\'s School</a> (co-educational day and boarding) in <a href="/wiki/Ashtead" title="Ashtead">Ashtead</a>, Surrey. The City of London School for Girls has its own preparatory department for entrance at age seven. It is the principal sponsor of The <a href="/wiki/City_Academy,_Hackney" title="City Academy, Hackney">City Academy, Hackney</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Academy,_Islington" title="City of London Academy, Islington">City of London Academy, Islington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Academy,_Southwark" title="City of London Academy, Southwark">City of London Academy, Southwark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The City is home to the <a href="/wiki/Cass_Business_School" title="Cass Business School">Cass Business School</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_London_Institute_of_Banking_%26_Finance" title="The London Institute of Banking &amp; Finance">The London Institute of Banking &amp; Finance</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Guildhall_School_of_Music_and_Drama" title="Guildhall School of Music and Drama">Guildhall School of Music and Drama</a> and parts of three of the <a href="/wiki/Universities_in_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Universities in London">universities in London</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Maughan_Library" title="Maughan Library">Maughan Library</a> of <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King&#39;s College London">King\'s College London</a> on <a href="/wiki/Chancery_Lane" title="Chancery Lane">Chancery Lane</a>, the business school of <a href="/wiki/London_Metropolitan_University" title="London Metropolitan University">London Metropolitan University</a>, and a campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Graduate_School_of_Business" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Chicago Graduate School of Business">University of Chicago Graduate School of Business</a>. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Law" title="University of Law">The College of Law</a> has its London campus in <a href="/wiki/Moorgate" title="Moorgate">Moorgate</a>. Part of <a href="/wiki/Barts_and_The_London_School_of_Medicine_and_Dentistry" title="Barts and The London School of Medicine and Dentistry">Barts and The London School of Medicine and Dentistry</a> is on the Barts hospital site at West Smithfield.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_libraries">Public libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Public libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Libraries operated by the Corporation include three lending libraries; Barbican Library, Shoe Lane Library and Artizan Street Library and Community Centre. Membership is open to all \xe2\x80\x93 with one official proof of address required to join.\n</p><p>Guildhall Library, and City Business Library are also public reference libraries, specialising in the history of London and business reference resources.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Author and journalist <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Shaxson" title="Nicholas Shaxson">Nicholas Shaxson</a> argued that, in return for the financial institutions  based in the City raising loans and finance for the British government, the City "has extracted privileges and freedoms from rules and laws to which the rest of Britain must submit". He further claims that the assistance provided to the institutions based within it, many of which help their rich clients with offshore tax arrangements, mean that the City is "a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> in its own right".<sup id="cite_ref-Shaxson_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shaxson-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table role="presentation" class="metadata mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px
